Automatically classifies tasks into compliance tiers and enforces appropriate verification.\n\n**Key Benefits**:\n- Single command replaces confusion between `sc:task` and `sc:task-mcp`\n- Automatic tier classification with confidence scoring\n- Appropriate verification for each task type\n- Prevents over-engineering for trivial changes\n- Ensures safety for critical changes\n\n## Triggers\n\nUse `/sc:task` when:\n- Task involves code modifications with downstream impacts\n- Complexity score >0.6 with code modifications\n- Multi-file scope (>2 estimated affected files)\n- Security domain paths detected (auth/, security/, crypto/)\n- Refactoring or system-wide changes requested\n\n**Auto-Suggest Keywords**:\n- High confidence: \"implement feature\", \"refactor system\", \"fix security\", \"add authentication\", \"update database schema\"\n- Moderate confidence: \"add new\", \"create component\", \"update service\", \"modify API\"\n\n## Usage\n\n```bash\n/sc:task [description]                           # Auto-detect all dimensions\n/sc:task [description] --compliance strict       # Force STRICT tier\n/sc:task [description] --compliance light        # Force LIGHT tier\n/sc:task [description] --skip-compliance         # Bypass compliance (escape hatch)\n/sc:task [description] --verify auto             # Auto-select verification\n```\n\n## Behavioral Flow\n\n### 0. Classification (Already Performed)\n\nClassification was handled by the `/sc:task` command before this skill was invoked. The tier has been determined and the classification header has been emitted. Proceed directly to execution based on the classified tier.\n\n**Reference** — the tier keyword tables (for context only, do not re-classify):\n- **STRICT**: security, authentication, database, migration, refactor, breaking change, encrypt, token, session, oauth\n- **EXEMPT**: explain, search, commit, push, plan, discuss, brainstorm\n- **LIGHT**: typo, comment, whitespace, lint, docstring, formatting, minor\n- **STANDARD**: implement, add, create, update, fix, build, modify, change (default)\n\n### 2. Confidence Display (Human-Readable)\n\nAfter the mandatory classification header, show a human-readable summary:\n\n```\n**Tier: STANDARD** [████████░░] 80%\n\nClassified as STANDARD:\n- Keywords matched: add, implement\n- Confidence score: 0.78\n- Considered alternatives: STRICT (0.35)\n```\n\nIf confidence <70%, add prompt: \"⚠️ Low confidence. Override with: `--compliance [strict|standard|light|exempt]`\"\n\n**Note**: The machine-readable header (Section 0) is for telemetry/A/B testing. This human-readable display is for user understanding.\n\n### 3. Execution Phase\n\nExecute task according to tier requirements:\n\n**STRICT Execution**:\n1. Activate project (mcp__serena__activate_project)\n2. Verify git working directory clean (git status)\n3. Load codebase context (codebase-retrieval)\n4. Check relevant memories (list_memories -> read_memory)\n5. Identify all affected files and test files\n6. Make changes with full checklist\n7. Identify all files that import changed code\n8. Update all affected files\n9. Spawn verification agent (quality-engineer)\n10. Run comprehensive tests: `pytest [path] -v`\n11. Answer adversarial questions\n\n**STANDARD Execution**:\n1. Load context via codebase-retrieval\n2. Search downstream impacts (find_referencing_symbols OR grep)\n3. Make changes\n4. Run affected tests OR document manual verification\n5. Verify basic functionality\n\n**LIGHT Execution**:\n1. Quick scope check (files/lines within bounds)\n2. Make changes\n3. Quick sanity check (syntax valid, no obvious errors)\n4. Proceed with judgment\n\n**EXEMPT Execution**:\n1. Execute immediately\n2. No verification overhead\n\n### 4. Verification Phase\n\nRoute to appropriate verification based on tier and paths:\n\n| Compliance Tier | Verification Method | Token Cost | Timeout |\n|-----------------|---------------------|------------|---------|\n| STRICT | Sub-agent (quality-engineer) | 3-5K | 60s |\n| STANDARD | Direct test execution | 300-500 | 30s |\n| LIGHT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n| EXEMPT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n\n**Critical Path Override**: Paths matching `auth/`, `security/`, `crypto/`, `models/`, `migrations/` always trigger CRITICAL verification regardless of compliance tier.\n\n**Trivial Path Override**: Paths matching `*.md`, `docs/`, `*test*.py` may skip verification.\n\n### 5. Feedback Collection\n\nAfter completion, collect implicit feedback:\n- Track if user overrode tier (implicit classification feedback)\n- Note smooth completion vs errors (quality signal)\n- Store for calibration learning\n\n## MCP Integration\n\n**Required Servers by Tier**:\n- STRICT: Sequential, Serena (fallback not allowed)\n- STANDARD: Sequential, Context7 (fallback allowed)\n- LIGHT: None required (fallback allowed)\n- EXEMPT: None required\n\n**Circuit Breaker Behavior**:\n- If required servers unavailable for STRICT tier, block task execution\n- For other tiers, use fallbacks with noted limitations\n\n## Tool Coordination\n\n**Planning Phase**:\n1. TodoWrite: Create task breakdown\n2. codebase-retrieval: Load context\n3. list_memories / read_memory: Check project state\n\n**Execution Phase**:\n1. Edit/MultiEdit/Write: Make changes\n2. Grep/Glob: Find references\n3. find_referencing_symbols: Trace dependencies\n\n**Verification Phase**:\n1. Task (quality-engineer): Spawn verification agent (STRICT only)\n2. Bash: Run tests directly (STANDARD)\n3. think_about_task_adherence: Reflect on completeness\n\n**Completion Phase**:\n1. write_memory: Save session state\n2. think_about_whether_you_are_done: Final check\n\n## Examples\n\n### STRICT Task\n```\n/sc:task \"implement user authentication with JWT\"\n\n-> Classified as STRICT (security domain, authentication keyword)\n-> Full 6-category checklist enforced\n-> Verification agent spawned\n-> Adversarial questions answered\n```\n\n### STANDARD Task\n```\n/sc:task \"add pagination to user list\"\n\n-> Classified as STANDARD (add keyword, typical feature)\n-> Context loaded before editing\n-> Downstream impacts checked\n-> Direct test execution\n```\n\n### LIGHT Task\n```\n/sc:task \"fix typo in README\"\n\n-> Classified as LIGHT (trivial classification\n-> Full verification enforced\n```\n\n## Boundaries\n\n**Will:**\n- Classify tasks into appropriate compliance tiers\n- Enforce tier-appropriate verification requirements\n- Provide confidence scoring with rationale\n- Track feedback for continuous calibration\n- Support user overrides with justification\n\n**Will Not:**\n- Skip safety-critical verification for STRICT tasks\n- Parallel execution vs Event-driven per-track execution\n\n---\n\n#### Phase 5: Synthesis — Merged Strategy Document\n**Goal**: Synthesize comparison results into a unified \"best of both\" strategy.\n\nTasks should:\n- Use `/sc:adversarial --depth deep` patterns to merge comparison verdicts\n- For each component area, define: the merged strategy, what to adopt from llm-workflows, what to keep from SuperClaude, what to discard from both, and the rationale\n- Apply the \"adopt patterns not implementation mass\" principle — extract control patterns, reject bloated machinery\n- Produce `merged-strategy.md` — the master document of merged approaches\n- Include a \"rigor without bloat\" section defining the efficiency constraints\n\n---\n\n#### Phase 6: Refactoring Plan Generation\n**Goal**: Convert merged strategy into concrete, actionable refactoring plans per SuperClaude component.\n\nTasks should:\n- Use `/sc:roadmap` patterns to convert strategy into implementation roadmap\n- For each SuperClaude component, produce a refactoring plan with:\n  - Specific file changes (file path, what to change, why)\n  - Priority tier (P0/P1/P2/P3)\n  - Effort estimate (XS/S/M/L/XL)\n  - Dependencies on other changes\n  - Acceptance criteria\n  - Risk assessment\n- Produce per-component `refactor-{component}.md` artifacts\n- Produce `refactor-master.md` — the unified cross-component plan with dependency graph\n\n---\n\n#### Phase 7: Validation & Adversarial Review\n**Goal**: Validate the refactoring plan through adversarial challenge.\n\nTasks should:\n- Use `/sc:adversarial` to debate the refactoring plan itself — is it complete? Is it over-engineered? Does it actually capture the llm-workflows rigor?\n- Use auggie MCP to verify all file references in the plan actually exist and the proposed changes are compatible with current code\n- Check for scope creep: does the plan stay within \"patterns not mass\"?\n- Check for missing connections: did any cross-framework insight get dropped?\n- Produce `validation-report.md` with pass/fail per plan item\n- Produce `final-refactor-plan.md` — the validated, corrected master plan\n\n---\n\n#### Phase 8: Sprint Checkpoint & Artifact Assembly\n**Goal**: Assemble all artifacts into a navigable deliverable and validate sprint completeness.\n\nTasks should:\n- Build `artifact-index.md` linking all 30+ produced artifacts\n- Verify traceability: every component in Phase 1 map → has strategy extraction → has comparison → appears in merged strategy → has refactoring plan\n- Verify no orphaned artifacts or dead references\n- Produce `sprint-summary.md` with: findings count, comparison verdicts, plan items by priority, estimated total effort, and recommended implementation order\n- Final quality gate: all artifacts pass structural validation\n\n---\n\n### Deterministic set to the appropriate repo root.\n- **R-RULE-02**: Phase sequencing is strict: no phase begins until the prior phase's checkpoint passes.\n- **R-RULE-03**: All comparison tasks must cite specific file:line evidence from both repos — no unsupported claims.\n- **R-RULE-04**: Anti-sycophancy check: every \"strength\" claimed must have a corresponding \"weakness\" or trade-off documented.\n- **R-RULE-05**: The \"adopt patterns not mass\" constraint must be verified in every Phase 6 refactoring plan item.\n- **R-RULE-06**: Artifacts are written to `.dev/releases/current/cross-framework-deep-analysis/artifacts/`.\n- **R-RULE-07**: Each phase ends with a checkpoint table verifying all acceptance criteria.\n\n### Compliance Tiers\n\n- **Phases 1-3**: EXEMPT (read-only analysis, no code changes)\n- **Phase 4**: STANDARD (comparison and debate, produces artifacts but no code changes)\n- **Phase 5**: STANDARD (synthesis, no code changes)\n- **Phase 6**: STRICT (refactoring plans that will drive code changes)\n- **Phase 7**: STRICT (validation of plans that will drive code changes)\n- **Phase 8**: LIGHT (assembly and verification)\n\n### MCP Requirements\n\nEvery task must specify MCP requirements. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01QZHKEMF3tfoL2qXioVTXsJ","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Strategy: LW Component — PABLOV Method\n     2→\n     3→**Component**: PABLOV Method (Programmatic Artifact-Based LLM Output Validation)\n     4→**Source**: `.gfdoc/rules/core/ib_agent_core.md`\n     5→**Path Verified**: true\n     6→**Strategy Analyzable**: true\n     7→**Generated**: 2026-03-14\n     8→\n     9→---\n    10→\n    11→## 1. What Is Rigorous About This Component\n    12→\n    13→PABLOV enforces a strict artifact-chain model where every stage of execution must produce a verifiable, machine-readable artifact before the pipeline proceeds. This eliminates \"vibes-based\" completion claims entirely.\n    14→\n    15→**Core rigor mechanisms:**\n    16→\n    17→- **Artifact chain completeness**: Five mandatory artifacts form an unbroken chain — `taskspec` (defines work), `expected_set` (defines batch), `worker_handoff` (claims completion), `qa_report` (validates claims), `programmatic_handoff` (proves work via filesystem evidence). No stage can be skipped. `ib_agent_core.md:106-112`\n    18→- **Agent Contracts**: Worker and QA are bound by formal contracts. Worker must complete items in `expected_set`, checkmark them in `taskspec`, and write `worker_handoff`. QA must validate item-by-item with filesystem verification and write `qa_report`. `ib_agent_core.md:87-97`\n    19→- **Zero-trust verification**: \"Audit by default, trust nothing\" — QA treats all Worker claims with skepticism and requires character-level verification for EXACT specifications. `ib_agent_core.md:99-104`\n    20→- **DNSP as a liveness guarantee**: The Detect-Nudge-Synthesize-Proceed protocol ensures the pipeline never permanently stalls on a missing artifact. Recovery is automatic. `ib_agent_core.md:103`\n    21→- **Five-Step Execution Pattern**: Every agent must follow READ → IDENTIFY → EXECUTE → UPDATE → REPEAT for each checklist item. Violations require task re-execution. `ib_agent_core.md:134-170`\n    22→\n    23→**Rigor verdict**: PABLOV's core insight — that LLM output can only be trusted when it is backed by programmatic, filesystem-verifiable artifacts — is sound and battle-tested. The distinction between \"claim\" (worker_handoff) and \"proof\" (programmatic_handoff) is particularly rigorous.\n    24→\n    25→---\n    26→\n    27→## 2. What Is Bloated / Slow / Expensive\n    28→\n    29→**Complexity overhead:**\n    30→- The five-artifact chain adds significant coordination overhead. Each batch requires creation, tracking, and validation of five separate artifact types.\n    31→- The mandatory sequential pattern (READ → IDENTIFY → EXECUTE → UPDATE → REPEAT, one item at a time) explicitly prohibits parallelism, even when items are independent. `ib_agent_core.md:141-170`\n    32→- The \"mandatory template usage protocol\" adds a full pre-write checklist before every file creation. `ib_agent_core.md:400-413`\n    33→\n    34→**Operational drag:**\n    35→- The bounded correction loop (max 5 per batch) means a single bad batch can cause 5 Worker re-executions + 5 QA re-executions before the system stops. `ib_agent_core.md:559-564`\n    36→- Session management overhead: proactive rollover at 375 messages or 175k tokens means long tasks routinely incur rollover cost even when no quality issue exists. `ib_agent_core.md:920-928`\n    37→\n    38→**Token/runtime expense:**\n    39→- Two full Claude sessions (Worker + QA) per batch. For a 50-item task with batch size 5: 10 Worker sessions + 10 QA sessions + potential correction sessions.\n    40→- `PABLOV_STRICT=false` by default — meaning if the programmatic handoff fails, the batch continues anyway. The rigor is therefore partially opt-in. `ib_agent_core.md:926`\n    41→- Synthesizing a `programmatic_handoff` from conversation mining is expensive (grep over JSONL, jq transforms). This is the fallback path, not the exception.\n    42→\n    43→**Maintenance burden:**\n    44→- Every new task type requires a template. The \"CATASTROPHIC FAILURE WARNING\" for missing templates indicates template compliance is fragile and high-friction. `ib_agent_core.md:401-413`\n    45→\n    46→---\n    47→\n    48→## 3. What Is Rigorous About This Component\n\nPABLOV enforces a strict artifact-chain model where every stage of execution must produce a verifiable, machine-readable artifact before the pipeline proceeds. This eliminates \"vibes-based\" completion claims entirely.\n\n**Core rigor mechanisms:**\n\n- **Artifact chain completeness**: Five mandatory artifacts form an unbroken chain — `taskspec` (defines work), `expected_set` (defines batch), `worker_handoff` (claims completion), `qa_report` (validates claims), `programmatic_handoff` (proves work via filesystem evidence). No stage can be skipped. `ib_agent_core.md:106-112`\n- **Agent Contracts**: Worker and QA are bound by formal contracts. Worker must complete items in `expected_set`, checkmark them in `taskspec`, and write `worker_handoff`. QA must validate item-by-item with filesystem verification and write `qa_report`. `ib_agent_core.md:87-97`\n- **Zero-trust verification**: \"Audit by default, trust nothing\" — QA treats all Worker claims with skepticism and requires character-level verification for EXACT specifications. `ib_agent_core.md:99-104`\n- **DNSP as a liveness guarantee**: The Detect-Nudge-Synthesize-Proceed protocol ensures the pipeline never permanently stalls on a missing artifact. Recovery is automatic. `ib_agent_core.md:103`\n- **Five-Step Execution Pattern**: Every agent must follow READ → IDENTIFY → EXECUTE → UPDATE → REPEAT for each checklist item. Violations require task re-execution. `ib_agent_core.md:134-170`\n\n**Rigor verdict**: PABLOV's core insight — that LLM output can only be trusted when it is backed by programmatic, filesystem-verifiable artifacts — is sound and battle-tested. The distinction between \"claim\" (worker_handoff) and \"proof\" (programmatic_handoff) is particularly rigorous.\n\n---\n\n## 2. What Is Bloated / Slow / Expensive\n\n**Complexity overhead:**\n- The five-artifact chain adds significant coordination overhead. Each batch requires creation, tracking, and validation of five separate artifact types.\n- The mandatory sequential pattern (READ → IDENTIFY → EXECUTE → UPDATE → REPEAT, one item at a time) explicitly prohibits parallelism, even when items are independent. `ib_agent_core.md:141-170`\n- The \"mandatory template usage protocol\" adds a full pre-write checklist before every file creation. `ib_agent_core.md:400-413`\n\n**Operational drag:**\n- The bounded correction loop (max 5 per batch) means a single bad batch can cause 5 Worker re-executions + 5 QA re-executions before the system stops. `ib_agent_core.md:559-564`\n- Session management overhead: proactive rollover at 375 messages or 175k tokens means long tasks routinely incur rollover cost even when no quality issue exists. `ib_agent_core.md:920-928`\n\n**Token/runtime expense:**\n- Two full Claude sessions (Worker + QA) per batch. For a 50-item task with batch size 5: 10 Worker sessions + 10 QA sessions + potential correction sessions.\n- `PABLOV_STRICT=false` by default — meaning if the programmatic handoff fails, the batch continues anyway. The rigor is therefore partially opt-in. `ib_agent_core.md:926`\n- Synthesizing a `programmatic_handoff` from conversation mining is expensive (grep over JSONL, jq transforms). This is the fallback path, not the exception.\n\n**Maintenance burden:**\n- Every new task type requires a template. The \"CATASTROPHIC FAILURE WARNING\" for missing templates indicates template compliance is fragile and high-friction. `ib_agent_core.md:401-413`\n\n---\n\n## 3. Execution Model\n\nThe PABLOV execution model is **sequential batch processing with dual-agent loops**:\n\n1. Orchestrator creates `taskspec` with checklist items\n2. Orchestrator generates `expected_set` (batch of N items from unchecked items)\n3. Worker agent executes items one-at-a-time, marks `[x]`, writes `worker_handoff`\n4. DNSP ensures `worker_handoff` exists (detect → nudge → synthesize)\n5. QA agent validates `worker_handoff` against filesystem, writes `qa_report`\n6. If QA fails: items unmarked, Worker receives `qa_report`, correction loop begins\n7. After QA pass: next batch created, cycle repeats\n\n**Quality enforcement**: Enforced at the artifact level (does the artifact exist? does the content match?) not at the intent level. This is a key design choice — programmatic over qualitative.\n\n**Extension points**:\n- `PABLOV_STRICT` flag: makes programmatic handoff failure fatal\n- `PABLOV_INCLUDE_DIFF`: adds git diffs to evidence\n- `PABLOV_FS_FILTER_BY_EVIDENCE`: filters filesystem changes by conversation evidence\n- `AGENT_PROMPT_OVERRIDE`: substitutes custom agent prompts\n- Task `assigned_to` field: auto-detects agent-specific prompts\n\n---\n\n## 4. Pattern Categorization\n\n**Directly Adoptable:**\n- The artifact-chain principle (claim → proof separation) is directly adoptable. The `worker_handoff` (claim) vs `programmatic_handoff` (filesystem proof) distinction is a pattern SuperClaude can adopt without the full machinery.\n- The five-step READ-before-EXECUTE enforcement is directly adoptable as a behavioral rule.\n- DNSP \"never wedge\" principle: always produce an artifact even if synthesized. Adoptable as a fallback guarantee.\n\n**Conditionally Adoptable:**\n- The dual Worker+QA loop is conditionally adoptable. The verification separation is sound, but the cost (two full sessions per batch) is high. A lighter verification pass (single session with self-check) would capture most of the value.\n- Agent Contracts (explicit output requirements per role) are adoptable in lighter form as structured delegation prompts.\n\n**Reject:**\n- The mandatory template pre-read checklist (catastrophic failure warning for every file write) is too high-friction for general use.\n- Sequential-only execution (explicit prohibition on parallel item execution) should be rejected; SuperClaude's parallel-first doctrine is more appropriate for independent items.\n- The full five-artifact chain is too heavy for single-session or lightweight tasks.\n","numLines":86,"startLine":1,"totalLines":86}}}

Applying P1/P2 learnings to the next milestone specification before execution begins addresses the most common failure mode in retrospective processes (findings are documented but not acted on).\n\n---\n\n## 2. This serializes milestone execution and adds calendar time.\n- Stage 3 decision point requires human judgment about which priority levels to address. This is intentional but adds latency to automated pipelines.\n\n**Token/runtime expense:**\n- The Stage 2 reflection prompt template is 60+ lines with 5 analysis dimensions and 4 priority tiers. The gap between the documented protocol and the actual manual process creates risk of incomplete execution.\n- Success metrics are defined but not automatically measured. Calculating \"issue recurrence rate\" requires manual comparison of M-X and M-X+1 retrospectives.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Execution Model\n\nThe protocol is a **human-in-the-loop retrospective pipeline**:\n\n1. **Stage 1**: Verify all completion conditions met\n2. **Stage 2**: `/sc:reflect` with deep analysis prompt → structured findings by priority\n3. **Stage 3**: Present to user → user selects priority levels to address\n4. **Stage 4** (if applicable): `/sc:design` → M-X.5 specification document\n5. **Stage 5** (if applicable): `/rf:taskbuilder` → M-X.5 task file\n6. **Stage 6**: `/sc:reflect` light review → M-X+1 amendments (required vs. recommended)\n7. **Stage 7a** (if applicable): `/rf:task` M-X.5 → await completion\n8. **Stage 7b**: `/rf:task` M-X+1 → begin next milestone\n\n**Quality enforcement**: The protocol enforces quality by requiring explicit documentation of failures, user-controlled scope of remediation, and mandatory forward propagation to prevent recurrence.\n\n**Extension points**:\n- Stage 6 review depth adjustable (light/deep/skip)\n- M-X.5 effort cap (suggested: 25% of original milestone)\n- Priority thresholds adjustable per project risk tolerance\n\n---\n\n## 4. Pattern Categorization\n\n**Directly Adoptable:**\n- Forward propagation (applying learnings from M-X to M-X+1 spec before execution) is directly adoptable as a standard step in SuperClaude's sprint workflow. This is the highest-value element.\n- The 4-condition completion checkpoint (tasks done + QA passed + deliverables verified + success criteria met) is directly adoptable as SuperClaude's sprint exit gate.\n- Priority-tiered findings (P1-P4) with explicit effort estimates per tier is directly adoptable for sprint retrospective reporting.\n\n**Conditionally Adoptable:**\n- The interim milestone concept (M-X.5) is conditionally adoptable for large sprint projects. For small sprints, inline fixes to the backlog are sufficient.\n- The user decision point at Stage 3 is conditionally adoptable — appropriate for human-supervised workflows, but would need automation for fully programmatic pipelines.\n\n**Reject:**\n- The 7-stage full process for every milestone. A compressed version (completion gate → key learnings → forward propagation) captures 80% of the value at 20% of the cost.\n- The requirement for separate M-X.5 task creation (full taskbuilder interview) for minor improvements. Direct specification amendments are sufficient for P3/P4 items.\n- The manual multi-command invocation model. The entire protocol should be automatable as a single SuperClaude sprint post-phase hook.\n","numLines":89,"startLine":1,"totalLines":89}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01Sc9uzm5SYLdz8YdRTCq9j5","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Strategy: LW Component — Anti-Hallucination Rules\n     2→\n     3→**Component**: Anti-Hallucination Rules\n     4→**Source**: `.gfdoc/rules/core/anti_hallucination_task_completion_rules.md`\n     5→**Path Verified**: true\n     6→**Strategy Analyzable**: true\n     7→**Generated**: 2026-03-14\n     8→\n     9→---\n    10→\n    11→## 1. What Is Rigorous About This Component\n    12→\n    13→This document defines a zero-tolerance protocol for preventing LLM fabrication. Its central innovation is inverting the default epistemic stance: claims are \"Incorrect\" by default, not \"Correct pending refutation.\"\n    14→\n    15→**Core rigor mechanisms:**\n    16→\n    17→- **Presumption of Falsehood**: Every claim starts with status \"Incorrect.\" The burden of proof lies entirely with the agent to verify every claim. Nothing is assumed true. `anti_hallucination_task_completion_rules.md:59-66`\n    18→- **Non-negotiable evidence format**: A claim cannot be \"Verified\" without a valid, accessible, relevant authoritative source. Format is explicit: `[Source: {authoritative_url}#{specific_section}]`. `anti_hallucination_task_completion_rules.md:67-74`\n    19→- **Zero-tolerance forgery penalty**: Fabricated URLs, dead links, or sources that fail to support the claim result in an immediate final FAS score of -100. Task fails with no exceptions. `anti_hallucination_task_completion_rules.md:76-82`\n    20→- **Mandatory negative evidence**: Failed verification attempts must be documented. \"Not found\" is a valid and required evidence entry. This prevents silence-as-success. `anti_hallucination_task_completion_rules.md:83-89`\n    21→- **Strict COMPLETE definition**: \"COMPLETE\" requires: all requirements satisfied, code integrated and functional, all warnings resolved (not suppressed), functionality tested, no dead code, all claims verified. `anti_hallucination_task_completion_rules.md:128-137`\n    22→- **Evidence table format**: Mandatory structured table with Claim, Status, Evidence/Justification, Source columns for all technical claims. `anti_hallucination_task_completion_rules.md:148-155`\n    23→\n    24→**Rigor verdict**: The Presumption of Falsehood + FAS -100 penalty for forgery creates genuine deterrence against confabulation. The mandatory documentation of negative evidence is particularly well-designed — it prevents agents from claiming \"I couldn't find anything\" without recording what was searched.\n    25→\n    26→---\n    27→\n    28→## 2. What Is Rigorous About This Component\n\nThis document defines a zero-tolerance protocol for preventing LLM fabrication. Its central innovation is inverting the default epistemic stance: claims are \"Incorrect\" by default, not \"Correct pending refutation.\"\n\n**Core rigor mechanisms:**\n\n- **Presumption of Falsehood**: Every claim starts with status \"Incorrect.\" The burden of proof lies entirely with the agent to verify every claim. Nothing is assumed true. `anti_hallucination_task_completion_rules.md:59-66`\n- **Non-negotiable evidence format**: A claim cannot be \"Verified\" without a valid, accessible, relevant authoritative source. Format is explicit: `[Source: {authoritative_url}#{specific_section}]`. `anti_hallucination_task_completion_rules.md:67-74`\n- **Zero-tolerance forgery penalty**: Fabricated URLs, dead links, or sources that fail to support the claim result in an immediate final FAS score of -100. Task fails with no exceptions. `anti_hallucination_task_completion_rules.md:76-82`\n- **Mandatory negative evidence**: Failed verification attempts must be documented. \"Not found\" is a valid and required evidence entry. This prevents silence-as-success. `anti_hallucination_task_completion_rules.md:83-89`\n- **Strict COMPLETE definition**: \"COMPLETE\" requires: all requirements satisfied, code integrated and functional, all warnings resolved (not suppressed), functionality tested, no dead code, all claims verified. `anti_hallucination_task_completion_rules.md:128-137`\n- **Evidence table format**: Mandatory structured table with Claim, Status, Evidence/Justification, Source columns for all technical claims. `anti_hallucination_task_completion_rules.md:148-155`\n\n**Rigor verdict**: The Presumption of Falsehood + FAS -100 penalty for forgery creates genuine deterrence against confabulation. The mandatory documentation of negative evidence is particularly well-designed — it prevents agents from claiming \"I couldn't find anything\" without recording what was searched.\n\n---\n\n## 2. What Is Rigorous About This Component\n    12→\n    13→Session management in llm-workflows is a proactive, dual-threshold system that prevents context overflow before it causes \"Prompt is too long\" failures, while preserving work-in-progress context across session boundaries.\n    14→\n    15→**Core rigor mechanisms:**\n    16→\n    17→- **Dual-threshold detection**: Session rollover triggered by EITHER message count (default 375, 87.5% of limit) OR token count (default 175,000, 87.5% of 200k). Using both prevents scenarios where few long messages exhaust tokens before the message count threshold triggers. `session_message_counter.sh:113-147`\n    18→- **Proactive vs. reactive rollover**: Rollover is checked BEFORE attempting `--resume`, not after failure. This eliminates \"Prompt is too long\" errors and context loss mid-batch. `session_message_counter.sh:114-116 comment`\n    19→- **Calibrated token estimation**: Python-based token counting with empirical constant `CHARS_PER_TOKEN = 2.8` (calibrated for technical content with code/paths/JSON). \"Using 2.8 to be slightly conservative.\" `session_message_counter.sh:103-108`\n    20→- **Context injection on rollover**: When rolling to new session, `generate_rollover_context()` creates a structured summary (batch state, completed items count, current role, workspace paths) that is prepended to the new session's prompt. `rollover_context_functions.sh:37-55`\n    21→- **Three rollover scenarios handled**: Proactive (threshold exceeded), emergency (context overflow error during execution), dead session recovery (session file exists but session is dead). `rigorflow_workflow_deep_dive_guide.md:622-630`\n    22→- **State file persistence**: Session IDs stored in `WORKER_SESSION_FILE`; removed on rollover to force new session creation. Prevents stale session resume. `session_message_counter.sh:170-171`\n    23→\n    24→**Rigor verdict**: The proactive dual-threshold approach is more rigorous than reactive rollover. Detecting overflow before it happens prevents data loss. The context injection mechanism ensures the new session is not starting blind.\n    25→\n    26→---\n    27→\n    28→## 2. What Is Bloated / Slow / Expensive\n    29→\n    30→**Complexity overhead:**\n    31→- Token estimation requires spawning a Python subprocess (via `estimate_session_tokens()`) for every pre-resume check. This is a non-trivial overhead for what is essentially a counting operation. `session_message_counter.sh:33-110`\n    32→- Two separate script files for session management, with some logic duplicated in the main orchestrator (inline rollover at `automated_qa_workflow.sh:4252-4297`). Architecture is split across three files.\n    33→- The `run_worker_with_message_check()` wrapper and `run_worker_with_rollover()` in `rollover_context_functions.sh` appear to be incomplete integrations (integration example code, not production paths). Actual rollover is handled inline in `automated_qa_workflow.sh`.\n    34→\n    35→**Operational drag:**\n    36→- Pre-resume session checks add a Python spawn + JSONL file read to every Worker invocation. For large tasks with many short batches, this overhead accumulates.\n    37→- The rollover context generation reads task file, counts completed items, queries batch state — multiple filesystem operations added to every rollover.\n    38→\n    39→**Token/runtime expense:**\n    40→- The `generate_rollover_context()` function produces a structured context block that is prepended to the new session prompt. This context itself consumes tokens in the new session. For a long task, rollover contexts can chain.\n    41→- Emergency rollover (from \"Prompt is too long\" error) requires retrying the same batch with a new session — doubling the cost of that batch.\n    42→\n    43→**Maintenance burden:**\n    44→- The `CHARS_PER_TOKEN = 2.8` constant requires re-calibration as content types change. The script comments note this was \"tested\" — but there is no automated test to detect drift.\n    45→- The rollover functions in `rollover_context_functions.sh` contain integration examples that appear aspirational rather than production-ready, creating confusion about what is actually used.\n    46→\n    47→---\n    48→\n    49→## 3. Execution Model\n    50→\n    51→Session management operates as a **pre-invocation health check** with an **automatic migration path**:\n    52→\n    53→1. Before each Worker (or QA) resume: read session file, check if session exists\n    54→2. If session exists: call `check_session_needs_rollover()` → count messages + estimate tokens\n    55→3. If rollover needed: generate context → clear session file → new session will be created\n    56→4. Worker invocation: if no session ID → create new session with rollover context prepended; if session ID → `--resume`\n    57→5. If context overflow error mid-execution: roll to new session without `--resume`, retry same batch\n    58→\n    59→**Quality enforcement**: Session management is a reliability mechanism, not a quality enforcement mechanism. It prevents pipeline failures due to context limits, but does not verify output quality.\n    60→\n    61→**Extension points**:\n    62→- `MAX_MESSAGES_PER_SESSION` and `MAX_TOKENS_PER_SESSION`: configurable thresholds\n    63→- Context generation is customizable — `generate_rollover_context()` can be modified to include additional state\n    64→- Three rollover scenarios are independent and can be handled differently per context\n    65→\n    66→---\n    67→\n    68→## 4. Pattern Categorization\n    69→\n    70→**Directly Adoptable:**\n    71→- The dual-threshold proactive rollover principle (check BEFORE resume, not after failure) is directly adoptable for SuperClaude's sprint CLI long-running pipelines.\n    72→- The calibrated 87.5% threshold (not 100%) with a safety buffer is directly adoptable as a general context management principle.\n    73→- Context injection on rollover (generate structured summary → prepend to new session prompt) is directly adoptable.\n    74→\n    75→**Conditionally Adoptable:**\n    76→- The Python-based token estimation is conditionally adoptable. The approach is sound; a more efficient implementation using native token counting APIs would be preferred.\n    77→- The state file-based session ID persistence (`WORKER_SESSION_FILE`) is conditionally adoptable for SuperClaude's sprint runner state management.\n    78→\n    79→**Reject:**\n    80→- The bash-based implementation with Python subprocesses for counting. What Is Rigorous About This Component\n    12→\n    13→The task builder is a structured 3-stage interview system that produces MDTM task files with self-contained checklist items designed to survive session rollovers.\n    14→\n    15→**Core rigor mechanisms:**\n    16→\n    17→- **Self-contained checklist items**: Every checklist item is a single, complete paragraph containing: action + WHY, integrated verification (\"ensuring...\" clause), output specification, error handling instruction, and completion gate. `taskbuilder.md:184-264`\n    18→- **Session rollover protection by design**: The v2 distinction over v1 is explicit — context loaded in batch 1 will NOT be available in batch 3+. Therefore every checklist item embeds all context it needs rather than referencing shared context. This is a structural solution to context window limitations. `taskbuilder.md:182`\n    19→- **Mandatory completion gate**: Every checklist item ends with \"This item cannot be marked as done until the actions are completed in their entirety exactly as described.\" `taskbuilder.md:270-272`\n    20→- **Pre-write silent validation checklist**: 7 checks before writing any task file, including YAML validity, section order, no nested checkboxes, self-contained check, integrated verification check, no standalone reads. `taskbuilder.md:315-324`\n    21→- **No standalone context-reading items**: Prohibited. Context must be embedded in action items. A standalone \"read context\" item is useless because that context is lost before it can be used. `taskbuilder.md:182, 356-358`\n    22→- **3-stage structured interview**: Stage 1 (core intent: goal, why, outputs, context), Stage 2 (phases and steps), Stage 3 (guardrails). Each stage has fixed wording to minimize cognitive load and prevent omissions. `taskbuilder.md:47-130`\n    23→- **Agent memory file**: `rf-task-builder/MEMORY.md` captures learned patterns (documentation tasks, planning tasks, batch size recommendations) that accumulate across conversations. `rf-task-builder/MEMORY.md:1-57`\n    24→\n    25→**Rigor verdict**: Self-contained checklist items are a significant innovation. The standard pattern (context item → action item → verification item) fails at scale because context from batch 1 is lost by batch 5. Embedding context in every action item eliminates this failure mode, at the cost of verbosity.\n    26→\n    27→---\n    28→\n    29→## 2. What Is Bloated / Slow / Expensive\n    30→\n    31→**Complexity overhead:**\n    32→- The 3-stage interview generates significant pre-task dialogue. For experienced users who know exactly what they want, the fixed interview structure adds friction.\n    33→- The synthesis rules (\"each step from Stage 2 → expand to 1-3 self-contained checkboxes\") can produce task files with dozens of items for moderate tasks, each with full embedded context. A 30-item task file may contain 30 copies of the same context references.\n    34→\n    35→**Operational drag:**\n    36→- The completion gate (\"This item cannot be marked as done until...\") in every item adds redundant text. In a 30-item task file, this phrase appears 30 times.\n    37→- \"Ensuring...\" verification clauses add a sentence to every item. Valuable but verbose at scale.\n    38→- Agent memory persistence means the task builder accumulates institutional knowledge but also accumulates potentially stale patterns that may not apply to new task types.\n    39→\n    40→**Token/runtime expense:**\n    41→- Self-contained items consume significantly more tokens than reference-based items. A task with 20 items where each item embeds 100 words of context = 2000 words of context duplication in the task file itself.\n    42→- The 3-stage interview, note appending between stages, and template reading before writing all add to task creation time.\n    43→\n    44→**Maintenance burden:**\n    45→- The template (`.gfdoc/templates/01_mdtm_template_generic_task.md`) is a large document (700+ lines). The builder must read it before writing every task file. `taskbuilder.md:400-410`\n    46→- Two templates exist (generic `01` and complex `02`), with different patterns. The builder must select between them. Selecting the wrong template produces a structurally incorrect task file.\n    47→- The MEMORY.md file grows over time without a pruning mechanism. Stale patterns accumulate.\n    48→\n    49→---\n    50→\n    51→## 3. Execution Model\n    52→\n    53→The task builder operates as an **interactive task specification system**:\n    54→\n    55→1. User invokes `/rf:taskbuilder_v2 [optional output path]`\n    56→2. Stage 1 interview: 4 fixed questions (goal, why, outputs, context) + optional single follow-up\n    57→3. Append Stage 1 notes to staging file before Stage 2\n    58→4. Stage 2 interview: phases (3-6) + steps per phase\n    59→5. Append Stage 2 notes before Stage 3\n    60→6. Stage 3 interview: 6 guardrail questions\n    61→7. Silent pre-write validation (7 checks)\n    62→8. Read template → expand stages into self-contained checklist items → write task file\n    63→9. Broadcast TASK_READY when complete\n    64→\n    65→**Quality enforcement**: Pre-write validation checklist ensures structural correctness before any file is written. The builder does NOT execute the task — it only creates the specification.\n    66→\n    67→**Extension points**:\n    68→- Stage 3 guardrails can be customized per task type\n    69→- Template selection (`01` generic vs `02` complex) based on task characteristics\n    70→- MEMORY.md captures and reuses optimal patterns for specific task types\n    71→- `RECOMMENDED_BATCH_SIZE` is included in TASK_READY message based on task complexity\n    72→\n    73→---\n    74→\n    75→## 4. Pattern Categorization\n    76→\n    77→**Directly Adoptable:**\n    78→- Self-contained checklist items (embed all context + action + verification + completion gate in a single item) is directly adoptable for SuperClaude sprint tasklist generation. This solves a real problem in multi-session sprint execution.\n    79→- The \"no standalone context-reading items\" rule is directly adoptable.\n    80→- The pre-write validation checklist is directly adoptable for SuperClaude's `/sc:tasklist` command output validation.\n    81→\n    82→**Conditionally Adoptable:**\n    83→- The 3-stage structured interview is conditionally adoptable for SuperClaude's `/sc:brainstorm` → `/sc:tasklist` workflow. The stages map to discovery → structure → constraints.\n    84→- The MEMORY.md pattern accumulation is conditionally adoptable — valuable for persistent agent memory, but requires pruning discipline.\n    85→\n    86→**Reject:**\n    87→- The mandatory 30-item completion gate repetition. A single completion gate policy in the task specification header is sufficient without repeating it in every item.\n    88→- The verbose template-reading requirement before every file creation. A cached template representation would reduce friction.\n    89→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. What Is Bloated / Slow / Expensive\n\n**Complexity overhead:**\n- The team lead must maintain per-track state and handle interleaved messages from multiple researchers. This is complex orchestration logic that introduces coordination bugs when message delivery is unreliable.\n- Spawning up to 15 agents (5 researchers + 5 builders + 5 executors) for maximum parallelism creates significant overhead in agent team initialization and cleanup.\n- The \"phased-parallel\" fallback (all researchers → all builders → all executors) synchronizes at each phase boundary, eliminating the fast-track advantage but adding three synchronization barriers.\n\n**Operational drag:**\n- Agent team creation requires `CLAUDE_CODE_EXPERIMENTAL_AGENT_TEAMS=1` flag — this is explicitly experimental infrastructure. `pipeline.md:7-13`\n- Each track creates separate task files with timestamped names. Maximum cost model for all agents. `rf-team-lead.md:1-30, rf-task-researcher.md:1-26`\n- Each agent in a 5-track pipeline has its own full context window. Memory overhead scales with track count.\n- Research notes files are written to disk per-track, then read by builders — filesystem I/O as a communication channel.\n\n**Maintenance burden:**\n- The \"EXPERIMENTAL\" label on the event-driven model means it has known reliability issues and may not work in all environments. Execution Model\n\nThe pipeline operates as an **event-driven multi-agent orchestration system**:\n\n**Single track**: Team lead → researcher (RESEARCH_READY) → builder (TASK_READY) → executor (EXECUTION_COMPLETE) → aggregate results\n\n**Multi-track**:\n1. Team lead spawns all researchers simultaneously\n2. As each RESEARCH_READY arrives: team lead reviews findings, immediately spawns that track's builder\n3. As each TASK_READY arrives: team lead immediately spawns that track's executor\n4. Each track progresses independently; fast tracks complete without waiting for slow tracks\n5. Team lead aggregates all EXECUTION_COMPLETE results when all tracks finish\n\n**Quality enforcement**: Quality is enforced by `automated_qa_workflow.sh` inside each executor, not by the pipeline orchestrator itself. The pipeline ensures execution; PABLOV ensures quality within each execution.\n\n**Extension points**:\n- Track count: 1-5 (configurable per request)\n- Template selection: per-track based on task complexity\n- Inter-agent communication protocol: extensible via message types\n- Fallback mode: configurable via coordination model selection\n\n---\n\n## 4. Pattern Categorization\n\n**Directly Adoptable:**\n- The event-driven per-track progression pattern (fast tracks not blocked by slow tracks) is directly adoptable for SuperClaude's `/sc:spawn` and parallel task delegation.\n- Track isolation (no cross-track agent communication) is directly adoptable as a sub-agent isolation rule.\n- The explicit documented fallback (event-driven → phased-parallel with known trigger conditions) is directly adoptable as SuperClaude's degradation strategy for parallel agent failures.\n\n**Conditionally Adoptable:**\n- The per-track state map maintained by the orchestrator is conditionally adoptable. Not a single recommendation — explicitly considers different solution scopes. `05_AUTOMATED_QA_FAILURE_DEBUGGING_SYSTEM_v2.md:564-566`\n- **Framework-level vs. project-level distinction**: The debugger explicitly analyzes \"a QA failure in the .gfdoc framework itself, not a user project.\" This scoping prevents false positives where framework issues are misdiagnosed as user errors. `05_AUTOMATED_QA_FAILURE_DEBUGGING_SYSTEM_v2.md:395`\n\n**Rigor verdict**: The 4-category scoring with explicit confidence levels transforms debugging from an ad-hoc process into a structured, reproducible one. The \"50% debugging time reduction\" and \"90%+ success rate\" claims are aspirational metrics from the spec, but the underlying design (pre-packaged context → classified failure → ranked solutions) is sound.\n\n---\n\n## 2. What Is Bloated / Slow / Expensive\n\n**Complexity overhead:**\n- The v2 scoring system (4 separate scores with grep pattern matching) versus the v1 simple if/elif chain introduces more complexity but similar practical classification power for the small number of known failure categories.\n- The diagnostic report format is highly detailed (~350 lines per report). For a simple execution pattern violation, most fields are not relevant.\n- The 3-solution requirement (surgical/systemic/hybrid) forces a solution framework even when one solution is clearly correct.\n\n**Operational drag:**\n- The debugging system is reactive — it only activates after 3 QA failures. By that point, the batch has failed 3 times, each failure consuming a Worker session + QA session + correction session. The system helps after significant waste has already occurred.\n- The manual invocation path (`troubleshoot.sh --qa-failure`) requires user awareness of the system's existence and correct usage.\n\n**Token/runtime expense:**\n- The diagnostic report itself (if comprehensive) is a large document that must be loaded into the debugging agent's context. Complex failures may produce reports exceeding 1000 lines.\n- The debugging agent reads `FRAMEWORK_DEBUGGING_GUIDE.md` + the diagnostic report + all referenced artifacts. Context load is substantial.\n\n**Maintenance burden:**\n- The grep-based pattern matching in `analyze_failure_pattern()` is fragile — QA report wording changes can break pattern detection. `05_AUTOMATED_QA_FAILURE_DEBUGGING_SYSTEM_v2.md:796-840`\n- Two versions exist (v1 and v2) in the backlog, with a separate reflection document. The production version is not clearly identified from file names alone.\n- The \"50% debugging time reduction\" and \"90%+ success rate\" metrics in the spec have no validation data cited in the document. These are targets, not measurements.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Execution Model\n\nThe failure debugging system operates as a **triggered diagnostic workflow**:\n\n1. `automated_qa_workflow.sh` detects max retry exceeded → calls `generate_diagnostic_report()`\n2. Report generator: collects failure evidence (QA report + handoffs + state + logs)\n3. Calls `analyze_failure_pattern()`: runs 4-category scoring → classifies failure with confidence\n4. Generates structured diagnostic report with failure summary, evidence, analysis, debugging prompt\n5. Reports output path + suggests: `cat report.md` OR invoke `/rf:framework-debug @report.md`\n6. Debugging agent (if invoked): reads report + FRAMEWORK_DEBUGGING_GUIDE.md → root cause analysis → 3 ranked solutions → test cases → documentation update recommendations\n\n**Quality enforcement**: The debugging system is a meta-quality mechanism — it enforces quality by detecting and classifying quality failures in the main workflow.\n\n**Extension points**:\n- Additional pattern categories can be added to `analyze_failure_pattern()`\n- Confidence thresholds are adjustable\n- Solution ranking criteria can be customized\n- Diagnostic report format can be extended with project-specific fields\n\n---\n\n## 4. Pattern Categorization\n\n**Directly Adoptable:**\n- The automatic trigger-after-N-failures pattern is directly adoptable for SuperClaude's sprint CLI: if a task fails N times, auto-generate a diagnostic context bundle.\n- The 4-category failure classification (execution, template, evidence, workflow) is directly adoptable as SuperClaude's sprint failure taxonomy.\n- Confidence scoring on failure classification (High/Medium/Low based on evidence weight) is directly adoptable.\n\n**Conditionally Adoptable:**\n- The pre-packaged artifact collection (gather all relevant evidence before analysis) is conditionally adoptable. In SuperClaude's context, this maps to: on task failure, collect (task file + prior outputs + error logs + execution state) into a diagnostic bundle.\n- The framework-vs-project diagnostic distinction is conditionally adoptable for sprint CLI: distinguish between \"the sprint runner failed\" (framework issue) vs. \"the task was poorly specified\" (user/spec issue).\n\n**Reject:**\n- The grep-based pattern matching in bash. In a Python sprint runner, regex matching on structured failure data is more reliable.\n- The 3-solution requirement as mandatory structure when a single fix is obvious.\n- Reactive-only triggering (after 3 failures). Proactive failure prevention (pre-execution confidence check) is more efficient — the confidence-check skill already implements this for SuperClaude.\n","numLines":86,"startLine":1,"totalLines":86}}}
